0.0,By the mid 1900s, psychotherapy became the most common cure, and many homosexuals spent countless hours being analyzed in hopes of changing their sexual preference (Dudley 125).
0.0,Dr. Evelyn Hooker, a heterosexual psychologist, conducted a ground-breaking study in the mid 1950s that went along similar reasoning as Freud.
0.0,In this courageous experiment, Hooker compared the psychological profiles of sixty men, half homosexual and half heterosexual.
0.0,She disagreed with the popular belief at the time that homosexuality was a mental illness, and concluded that there was no significant psychological difference between homosexual and heterosexual men; gay men were no more insane than their straight counterparts (Marcus 183).
0.0,gay
0.0,Documented homosexuality dates as far back as ancient Greece and other cultures of the time, where it was considered to be a very normal and natural occurrence (Emond).
0.0,Fortunately, many prominent psychiatrists also believed that homosexuality was not an illness, and their lobbying, along with the innovative study performed by Hooker, who has been referred to as the Rosa Parks of the gay movement convinced the American Psychiatric Association Board of Trustees to vote to remove homosexuality from the Diagnostic and Statistical Manual as a mental illness in December of 1973.
0.0,the Rosa Parks of the gay movement
0.0,Just over a year later, the American Psychological Association also removed homosexuality from their list of mental illnesses (Marcus 11).
0.0,The American Psychological Association further reiterated this belief when an overwhelming majority of the Council of Representatives adopted the Resolution on Appropriate Therapeutic Responses to Sexual Orientation in 1997, which publicly chastised those who attempted to cure homosexuality by means of various forms of treatment.
0.0,cure
0.0,It stated, rather that homosexuality was merely a difference in the opinion and values of the common person, but must still be respected as an individual orientation, and thus treated as one (Resolution on Appropriate Therapeutic Responses to Sexual Orientation).
0.0,Perhaps one of the most famous studies on this topic was concluded in 1991 by Michael Bailey, an assistant professor of psychology at Northwestern University, and Richard Pillard, an associate professor of psychiatry at Boston University School of Medicine, and found that sexual orientation in males is largely due to genetics.
0.0,For two years, these men studied the number of occurrences of homosexuality in both monozygotic, or identical twins (a set of twins coming from the same fertilized egg and thus having identical DNA), and dizygotic, or fraternal twins (a set of twins from too separate zygotes, causing them to have similar DNA, but not any more so than that of two ordinary siblings), in addition to adoptive brothers of gay males (meaning that all of these males would have been raised in the same environment).
0.0,In his book The Symposium, Plato wrote Those who are halves of a man whole pursue males, and being slices, so to speak, of the male, love men throughout their boyhood, and take pleasure in physical contact with men (qtd. in Isay 11).
0.0,In total, 110 pairs of twins (identical and fraternal) and 142 sets of male and their adopted brothers were studied, where at least one of the two had been classified as homosexual, either by self-identification or other means.
0.0,Those who are halves of a man whole pursue males, and being slices, so to speak, of the male, love men throughout their boyhood, and take pleasure in physical contact with men
0.0,Out of the 56 homosexual males who had identical twins, 29, or approximately 52 % of their identical twin brothers were also found to be homosexual, as compared to only 12, or approximately 22 % of the 54 non-identical twins of homosexual males, and 6, or approximately 11 % of the 57 adopted brothers of homosexual males who were unrelated in terms of genetics.

0.0,I think plenty of brands have heard the siren call of Facebook ads.
0.0,The ability to target your demo is really terrific, but you're in danger of creating a relationship with fans that ultimately is built on a "what have you done for me lately" foundation.

0.0,This sets up a pattern where the consumer now expects to be rewarded for being your fan with a tangible item, that is, free stuff.
0.0,That's not a bonus item, it's now a standard part of the agreement.
0.0,Want me as a fan?
0.0,Give me free stuff.
0.0,The point of Social Media isn't to distribute coupons and a real fan wants to engage with a brand for a whole host of reasons, often free / discounted product is the least of these reasons.

0.0,I think when used properly they can be terrific.
0.0,What do I mean by used properly?
0.0,As a reward for people who have engaged with the brand in a meaningful way.
0.0,Send us a picture of you wearing a brand t-shirt and sure, you've earned a free sandwich.
0.0,Recruit some friends and I'm happy to give you all some coupons.
0.0,But when fans enter the relationship feeling they are entitled to free samples and you're in trouble.

0.0,Prosperity has brought with it a new emphasis on historic preservation.
0.0,Dublin excels in packaging its past for the visitor.
0.0,You can view artifacts from the Bronze Age, trace the history of the Easter Rising, or revisit Leopold Blooms odyssey in Ulysses.
0.0,Old buildings are being recycled; for example, the 17th-century Royal Hospital now holds the Museum of Modern Art.
0.0,And Dublin, a city large in expectations, is still small enough for the visitor to see most of its sights on foot.
0.0,New construction is everywhere, the streets buzz, traffic is increasingly congested, and in the frenetic pace of rush hour everyone in Dublin seems intent on changing places with everyone else.
0.0,City on the Liffey
0.0,The River Liffey flows from west to east through the center of the city to Dublin Bay.
0.0,The river forms a natural line between the north and south sections of the city.
0.0,Historically and culturally this north-south distinction has always been significant, and it still is today, with a dose of good-humored rivalry between the two areas.
0.0, I never go north of the Liffey,
0.0, I never go north of the Liffey, one man remarked.
0.0,Farther out, both north and south, are the sweeping curves of the Royal and Grand Canals.
0.0,The occasional cry of gulls and unexpected distant vistas will remind you that Dublin is by the sea, and the Wicklow mountains, which hold Dublin closely to the coast, are visible from everywhere.
0.0,Dublin is an intimate city, physically small but tightly packed, a perfect place for walking.
0.0,College Green, the home of Trinity College, provides a natural focus just south of the OConnell Street bridge.
0.0,OConnell Street, the citys grand boulevard, leads north to Parnell Square.
0.0,Dublin and the Dubliners
0.0,To the south and east is St. Stephens Green and Georgian Dublin where the national museums are located.
0.0,Along the Liffey to the west is Temple Bar, center of nightlife and home to many of Dublins cutting-edge artists and artistic endeavors.
0.0,Up the hill from Temple Bar are Dublin Castle and Christ Church Cathedral.
0.0,It wont rain on you in Dublin all the time.
0.0,The climate here can best be described as changeable and yet the sudden shifts from light to dark, sunshine to shower, are part of the citys magic.
0.0,Buildings seem to transform themselves depending on the light; Dublin under a lowering sky is a different place from Dublin in sunshine.
1.0,Enjoying Dublin
0.0,Joyce, the high priest of literary Modernism, imagined and interpreted Dublin for the world in Ulysses (youll see references to it all over).
0.0,At night the streets are crowded with people bent on having a good time.
0.0,Beckett and Joyce, among others, had to leave their homeland to understand itand to be understood.
0.0,The citys impact on the rock and pop music scene with the likes of U2 and Bob Geldof is well knowntheres even a self-guided tour of their haunts.
0.0,Traditional Irish music is also alive and well, especially in the pubs, and there has been a revival of storytelling, poetry reading, and traditional dancing.
0.0,And in this city, where literature and theater have historically dominated the scene, visual arts are finally coming into their own with the new Museum of Modern Art and the many galleries that display the work of modern Irish artists.
0.0,Prosperity is in the air; the roar of the Celtic Tiger can clearly be heard.
0.0,And while multinational chains have made inroads, they seem less blatant here than elsewhere.
0.0,Many shops, and also hotels and guest houses, have been owned and managed by the same families for years, and theirs is the welcome of traditional Dublin hospitality.
0.0,Dublins food has undergone a metamorphosis.
0.0,There was a time when you might have apologized for it, but no longer.
0.0,Dublin has international restaurants galore, and the New Irish Cuisine is built upon fresh products of Irelands seas, rivers, and farms.
0.0,But this is not the whole picture.
0.0,Coffee has replaced the ubiquitous teaDublin is now almost as much a coffee city as Vienna or Seattle.
0.0,City and Countryside
0.0,In a city of such human proportions it is not surprising that parks and gardens abound for recreation and relaxation.
0.0,The proverbial hospitality and warm welcome are still here.
0.0,Phoenix Park in the northwest is the largest open space, but squares like St. Stephens Green are the garden oases of the city.
0.0,As capital of Europes most explosive economy, Dublin seems to be changing before your very eyes.
0.0,On the coast, Sandymount, Dollymount, and Killiney strands are the places to go.
0.0,The beautiful Wicklow Mountains, and the Wicklow Mountains National Park provide a more rugged countryside, and the area has breathtaking houses and gardens such as Castletown, Mount Usher, and Powerscourt.
0.0,To the north and west are the ancient sites of Ireland: Malahide Castle, the evocative hill of Tara, and the long barrows of Knowth and Newgrange.
0.0,This busy, modern European city sits on a thousand years of historyhistory is present everywhere, from elegant Merrion Square to the bullet holes on the General Post Office.
0.0,The DART (Dublin Area Rapid Transit) runs north and south along the coast.
0.0,Its an ideal way for the visitor to reach outlying sights and villages.
0.0,There are many guided bus tours to sights outside the city, and some are accessible by city bus.
0.0,Young at Heart?
0.0,Dublin is a young city.
0.0,Almost half of Irelands population is under twenty-five, and with its universities and professional schools, Dublin also has a large student population.
0.0,The universities attract students from all over the world, and this influx helps to make Dublin a busy, buzzing international city.
0.0,However, young and old, stranger and Dubliner rub shoulders quite happily.
0.0,Religion and respect for parents has not yet gone out of fashion.
0.0,And young graduates are not leaving nowmultinational corporations and European Union investment mean there are plenty of opportunities for them at home.
0.0,Unemployment is at an all-time low.
0.0,The Irish are actually beginning to come home.
0.0,Its also a city of the imagination, reinvented and reappraised in the literature of its exiles.
0.0,And the old Dublin is with us, toothe irreverent city of wit and charm and that peculiar magic possessed by Ireland and the Irish.
0.0,Today Hong Kong remains a capitalist enclave with its laws and rights intact, and China has promised that Hong Kong will continue in this fashion for at least 50 years.
0.0,Beijings announced policy of maintaining Hong Kongs prosperity and stability makes sense.
0.0,Hong Kong has long been Chinas handiest window on the West, and the city is unrivaled in its commercial know-how and managerial expertise.
0.0,Around the time of the transition there was much speculation about how things would change.
0.0,But in fact, once news of the handover vanished from the front pages, the people of Hong Kong returned to their usual topics of conversation: the economy and the price of housing.
0.0,With its vibrant atmosphere and night-and-day activity it is an intoxicating place.
0.0,The impression of the visitor today will be that very little has changed.
0.0,Establishments are no longer called Royal, Queen Elizabeth has vanished from the coinage, and the Union Jack has been replaced by the flag of China and the new Hong Kong flag with its bauhinia flower.
0.0,But in fact, there have been changes, many of them due to economic progress, new construction, and other factors that influence cities all over the world.
0.0,Others are more subtle.
0.0,British social customs are still evident in the kind of polite service you get in hotels and in the long lines of people waiting for buses at rush hour.
0.0,The British population has decreased; today there are as many American and Australian ex-pats as there are British.
0.0,With a population of nearly eight million and a total area of just over 1,095 square km (423 square miles), housing is one of Hong Kongs perennial nightmares.
0.0,Hong Kong is crowdedit has one of the worlds greatest population densities.
0.0,To alleviate the problem, the government has become the citys major landlord with the construction of massive apartment blocks that, though they have every modern facility, average only 9 square m (100 square ft) in size.
0.0,Hong Kong and Its People
0.0,Whole cities have been created in the New Territories, although the unimaginative architecture of these towns has been criticized.
0.0,Of Hong Kongs population, 98 percent are Chinese.
0.0,The Chinese people have been described as hardworking and pragmatic, attitudes that have contributed to Hong Kongs success.
0.0,There are many stories of refugees who arrived with nothing in their pockets, set up a small sidewalk stall, worked diligently until they had their own store, and then expanded it into a modest chain.
0.0,But it is also efficient, with one of the best transportation systems anywhere, and for such a crowded place, quietyou dont hear voices raised in anger, motorists sitting on their horns, or loud boomboxes.
0.0,Old customs are still followed: Fate and luck are taken very seriously, and astrologers and fortune-tellers do a steady business.
0.0,Before a skyscraper can be built, a feng shui (see page 68) investigation must take place to ensure that the site and the building will promote health, harmony, and prosperity.
0.0,Youll also notice that gambling is a passion, whether it be cards, mah-jong, the lottery, or the horses.
0.0,Hong Kong has two major racetracks as well as an intensive off-track betting system, and on weekends the ferries to Macau are crowded with people on their way to the casinos.
0.0,Sightseeing in Hong Kong starts at sea level with the enthralling water traffica mix of freighters, ferries, tugs, junks, and yachts.
0.0,From Victoria Peak, Hong Kongs highest point, or from skyscrapers and hotels, they are especially exciting at night when the lights are on.
0.0,The business and financial center and the signature soaring architecture are on Hong Kong Island.
0.0,Across Victoria Harbor, connected by ferry and the MTR rail line, is the Kowloon peninsula with its hotels, nightlife, and almost non-stop shopping.
0.0,Beyond, in the New Territories, are a mixture of high-rise suburban towns, ancient sites and walled villages, country parks, and farms with ducks and fish ponds.
0.0,Hong Kongs other, less developed islands, Lantau, Lamma, and Cheung Chau, provide getaways.
0.0,You can also take a ferry to Macau to find an entirely different kind of city, a unique blend of Chinese and Iberian culture.
0.0,Its anyones guess what may happen in the future, but for now Hong Kong bristles with energy and ambition, and for the visitor, this beautiful city with its contrasts and variety is an exhilarating experience.
0.0,Shopping never endstheres always another inviting spot just down the street.
0.0,Youll find Hong Kong easy to get around, the people helpful, English spoken everywhere, and food that lives up to its reputation.
0.0,Exciting, mysterious, glamorousthese words have described Hong Kong for at least a century.
0.0,On 1 July, 1997 the British Crown Colony of Hong Kong reverted to Chinese sovereignty as a Special Administrative Region of the Peoples Republic of China.

0.0,The Chinese legend of Madame White Snake, the snake demon that takes human form and becomes the wife of a man, has exerted a lasting influence over East Asian folktales and fiction for centuries.
0.0,But over time, characterizations of her became more complex, and the persona of Madame White Snake became more sympathetic, and perhaps even a model of the ideal Confucian wife, particularly in Pagoda.

0.0,While both stories each characterize Madame White Snake fairly consistently within their narratives, the uneven characterization in film noir perhaps mirrors the evolution of her character over time: readers may not be sure whether she is a pure villainess or whether she is a good wife who is badly treated by society, because there is evidence of both throughout her legend.
0.0,She is a loyal wife to her husband as she has promised, but she also causes him to find trouble with the law and deceives him about her supernatural nature.

0.0,PRESCRIPTION PRIVILEGES MAKE SOME PSYCHOLOGISTS ANXIOUS
0.0,The APA has spent more than $1 million to help state psychological associations develop and lobby for such prescription privileges -- or "RxP" -- legislation.
0.0,A total of 31 state psychology associations have task forces dedicated to developing and lobbying for prescription-privileges legislation.

0.0,Critics say that is not nearly enough compared with other prescribers, such as M.D. psychiatrists or nurse practitioners who have at least six years' medical education and clinical experience.

0.0,Also, international competitors drew on a large supply of very cheap labor.
0.0,Jobs were scarce in other steel-exporting countries, and labor laws were either non-existent or allowed employers to pay much less for work.
0.0,Labor costs in America continued to go up, draining US companies of their resources, while companies overseas were able to cut labor costs and put that money back into updating and renovating their facilities.
0.0,On a worldwide scale, newer materials such as aluminum, plastic, and composites were beginning to substitute steel both at home and abroad.
0.0,Steel demand worldwide was beginning to decline, and it affected both domestic and foreign companies.
-1.0,However, to American companies already suffering financial setbacks, outdated machinery, and fierce competition, this lack of demand was an inconvenience they could not afford.
0.0,Americas steel remained unsold, flooding the world market with inferior products that no one wanted to buy.
0.0,Since this problem was a national one rather than a local one, the problems that were occurring in Youngstown were not unique.
-1.0,Youngstown was perhaps hit harder than any other town by the collapse of the steel industry, but it was not alone.
-1.0,The problem was a national one, involving many more mills and issues than Youngstowns alone.
0.0,J. Philip Richley, a union member and organizer of many attempts to save 5the mills, has summed it up thus: You just cant solve a nation-wide problem in a single city.
0.0,You just cant solve a nation-wide problem in a single city.
0.0,The decline of the world steel market affected not just Youngstown but the entire steel community in America.
0.0,Trying to prop up one citys mills was impossible when faced with the depression that spread throughout the entire industry.
0.0,The Save Our Valley Campaign: Lack of Funds and Plans
0.0,Eventually, some religious leaders involved in the Ecumenical Coalition joined forces within community members and former steel mill employees to create the Save Our Valley Campaign.
0.0,As the name suggests, local leaders wanted to instill the people of Youngstown with a fierce sense of urgency, driving them forward to confront steel companies and owners and help secure the future of the region.
0.0,The events that would follow this date (known as Black Monday) are seen by the people who witnessed them either as stories of great courage and determination or as monuments to human failure and false hope.
0.0,Marches, speeches, and letter writing were all employed to help stimulate the Campaign and rally the people.
0.0,But the Campaign was bogged down heavily by the lack of proper funding.
-1.0,The people of Youngstown, being now unemployed had very little money to spend on anything but staying alive.
0.0,College tuition, clothes, food, and heating all had to come before donations to non-profit organizations.
0.0,People outside of the area had no personal investment in the mills, and so it was difficult to convince anyone from out of the county to contribute funds.
0.0,The lack of money proved to be crippling, because it prevented the organizations involved from purchasing the mills to run collectively.
-1.0,Without funds, the Save Our Valley Campaign could do nothing major to help salvage the citys dying economy.
-1.0,The Save Our Valley Campaign also lacked one essential component: an actual concrete plan.
-1.0,No one seemed to know just how to go about fixing the problems.
0.0,Letters and petitions were all very well, but they did little to improve the situation.
0.0,People clung to vague ideas of worker collectivization, but no one could really fathom exactly how that would work; the people of Youngstown were, after all, not particularly familiar with socialism or collectivization in general.
-1.0,Beyond that, no one knew how they should proceed: everyone knew that saving the mills was important, but nobody stepped forward with a full-fledged plan to do it without losing huge amounts of money and dragging even more people down.
0.0,Without funds to drive the efforts, or even a real plan of action, the Save Our Valley Campaign did more harm than good.
0.0,In effect, it raised the hopes of workers without having any real chance at saving anything.
0.0,People became excited and waited for the mills to reappear, but they never did.
-1.0,The Campaign failed to save any jobs and Youngstown was plunged into economic chaos.
0.0,The Apathy of USWA
0.0,United Steel Workers of America was the union representing the Youngstown steel workers when the closings hit.
0.0,Initially many assumed that their union would take a lead role in fighting for the recovery of their jobs.
0.0,However, it soon became clear that although the local union leaders were prepared to fight, the international branch was not.
0.0,Rather than sit back and wait for their jobs to be snatched away, the workers and local union members in the mills fought long and hard to be able to keep the factories open.
-1.0,The higher levels of the union became increasingly disassociated with Youngstown and its plight, attempting to shut out the appeals from workers and local union representatives and to ignore what was really happening.
0.0,Actually, one main reason for the behavior of the USWA was that union leaders really had no idea what to do.
0.0,No one had ever seen a shutdown of this magnitude and rapidity before, and none of the leaders of USWA, not even president Lynn Williams, knew what could be done.
0.0,It was clear to everyone that the economic fallout from this series of closings would be one of the worst in US history, and so without any real precedents the union leaders were flustered.
0.0,Rather than try and come up with some sort of scenario, the USWA simply ignored what was going on in Youngstown, hoping that perhaps the problem would resolve itself, or at least not spread any further than it already had.
0.0,Besides incompetence, the USWA had one other major reason for rejecting their local counterpart: fear of socialism.
0.0,Obviously the union itself was not afraid of socialist action, but they worried that the federal government might see the efforts of Youngstown workers to collectivize as a movement towards socialism and perhaps even communism.
0.0,If the USWA supported the efforts to revive the mills and encouraged worker control and ownership of the factories, then the government (and potentially other important people and institutions as well) might begin to think that the UWSA leaders were encouraging socialism.
0.0,This would mean that UWSA would lose credibility with the American government and its people, something they could not afford to do.
0.0,Therefore, they decided to withdraw support and let the local branch fight it out alone.
0.0,Regionalism
0.0,From its very first days the Mahoning Valley has been an area packed with small villages and hamlets.
0.0,Youngstown is the name of the major city area, but surrounding it on all sides are small communities which to the casual viewer are indistinguishable from the main city itself.
-1.0,Petitions, protests, rallies, collectivization, and even the takeover of a steel companys headquarters were all attempted in a desperate movement by those in the industry to preserve the only source of employment that this town had.
0.0,Boardman, Poland Township, Struthers, Lowellville, Warren, Lordstown, Canfield, Niles, and many other towns and districts are crowded around Youngstown (see Figure 3).
0.0,People from each town work, shop, eat, and socialize in towns separate from their own, making each town strongly dependent on every other town.
0.0,However, although traffic is heavy between each separate district, each area has its own distinct cultural ethnicity, educational system, heritage, history, and even food.
0.0,For example, Struthers is a poor town with a large Slovak population, where education is generally better than in surrounding towns, but unemployment is much higher and pollution is widespread.
0.0,Most people in Struthers are either Orthodox or Baptist.
0.0,Two blocks over one finds Boardman, a well-off township with a reputation for rich but unsuccessful schools.
0.0,Its residents are mainly Italian and Roman Catholic, with a small concentration of Methodists on the east side.
0.0,Unemployment is low in comparison with surrounding towns, and the streets are clean and well kept.
0.0,With many more cultures, religions, and economic levels living in close proximity to one another, a curious phenomenon has overtaken the area: regionalism.
0.0,Each town, with their own identity, instills a strong regionalistic feeling within their respective populations, which dictates many habits, exchanges, and interactions between populations.
-1.0,Oftentimes this regionalism takes the form of bizarre forms of hatred, with certain towns becoming sworn enemies of others.
0.0,With so much regional tension, it became very hard for workers to unite under a common cause, even one that would save their jobs and their futures.
0.0,Workers from Poland Township would refuse to attend rallies with workers from Campbell, and citizens of Struthers would become suspicious of people from Boardman, even if they were supposed to be working towards the same thing.
0.0,A lack of cooperation became a crippling problem for the movement, because no one was willing to put aside regional differences to work together.
0.0,In some instances, small companies would express interest in helping the movement or in relocating their business in the area, but because of regional pride no one could ever agree where the new businesses should relocate.
0.0,In this way the people of the Mahoning Valley missed many opportunities for new industrial or commercial lifeblood because of arbitrary arguments where the goal was simply to protect regional pride.
-1.0,These well-intentioned efforts ultimately failed, leaving thousands with shattered dreams and a distinct lack of trust in fellow humankind.
0.0,Conclusion: The Aftershock and the Significance of Black Monday
-1.0,Black Monday was a devastating blow to an entire generation of people.
0.0,The efforts to avoid catastrophe after the fact were unsuccessful for four main reasons: the failure of the international steel market, the lack of funds and plans in initiatives such as the Save Our Valley Campaign, the refusal of the USWA to support their local chapter out of ineptitude and fear, and the absurd but very real regionalism which corrupted solidarity efforts and drove away any hope for brining in new companies.
0.0,What happened in Youngstown may not seem significant on an international or even on a national level, and perhaps it is not.
0.0,But to the thousands of people living there, the loss of the mills was a devastating event that sent shock waves through their economic, political, and social futures.
-1.0,Because of the mills and their conspicuous absence, hundreds of people were uprooted, forced to leave their homes and tightly knit communities.
0.0,Hundreds more joined the unemployment lines, or even began living on the streets.
0.0,For the people of Youngstown, Black Monday was not just a historical event- it was the most important event in their lives.
0.0,The steel workers who tried to save their jobs and their lives were part of something greater than themselves, something which would endure long after they had moved away and moved on.
0.0,Even though they eventually failed, the fact that they tried to preserve what they felt belonged to them is an amazing example of how far people will go to save their lives and the futures of their children.
0.0,But why did the brave attempts by union leaders and concerned citizens to revive the steel industry ultimately fail?
0.0,An Extended Essay in History
0.0,When examining the areas history, culture, and economic situation we can identify four main reasons: the refusal of the international leadership of United Steelworkers of America to support their unions Youngstown branch, the lagging international steel market, the lack of a clear, organized vision for individual initiatives such as the Save Our Valley Campaign, and crippling regionalism which caused animosity between different small towns in the region, all contributed in some way to the failure of the workers and union leaders to save the industry.
0.0,Most importantly, the problem in Youngstown was a nationwide problem.
0.0,Although it affected Youngstown and the surrounding area more than it affected other regions, the local people simply could not solve a national crisis on a local level.
0.0,A Brief History of Steel in Northeastern Ohio
0.0,In 1802 James and Daniel Heaton discovered ore and coal lining Yellow Creek in an area outside of Youngstown known as Poland Township.
0.0,Their blast furnace, Hopewell, was the very first blast furnace in the area.
0.0,During the Civil War, Youngstown played a vital role in supplying the Union army with iron products.
0.0,Youngstown also was a major railway crossroads, due to its strategic position between Cleveland, Pittsburgh, New York, and Chicago.
0.0,The Decline of the Northeastern Ohio Steel Market: Why Did Attempts by Union Leaders and Concerned Citizens to Revive the Steel Industry Ultimately Fail?
0.0,In fact, More rail cars passed under the Center Street Bridge [a major bridge in Youngstown] per day than any other location in the country.
0.0,During the 19th century, the center of iron manufacturing had gradually shifted from the far East Coast (Massachusetts and Eastern Pennsylvania) to the Ohio Valley Pittsburgh regions of the Northeast, including the Mahoning Valley and the Hanging Rock region of Ohio and Kentucky.
0.0,By 1880, Youngstowns population had grown to nearly 16,000, which meant it had doubled in size over a twenty-year period.
0.0,The town continued to prosper, driven by the flux of immigrants pouring in with the hopes of employment at the mills.
0.0,This prosperity continued until the late 1920s, when the Great Depression hit the area hard.
0.0,Despite the Congress of Industrial Organizations successful efforts to establish a national steel workers union, the industry barely survived the Depression years.
0.0,Finally, the outbreak of the Second World War made iron and steel important again, and Youngstown was bolstered out of its economic standstill into a fast-paced period of booming growth.
0.0,Strikes racked the town during the forties, fifties, and sixties, and they were often long and bloody.
0.0,In 1973, the Experimental Negotiating Agreement was signed.
-1.0,This prohibited strikes and lockout, angering workers and driving productivity and laborer morale down.
0.0,At the same time, stricter governmental standards for environmental protection and the growth of imported steel were making it harder to produce and market American steel parts, and the overeager shareholders in the companies stock were pushing for more and more of their share of the pie.
0.0,Most importantly, Youngstowns steel mills were slowly becoming less efficient and more expensive.
0.0,September 19, 1977 is a date that few people in Youngstown, Ohio will ever forget.
0.0,Old technology was not replaced, obsolete methods were not updated, and almost none of the industrys profits were being utilized to help modernize.
0.0,Black Monday and the Crash of the Steel Industry
0.0,The announcement of the closing of the mills in 1977 was the beginning of a downward spiral, which would send the entire valley into chaos and ruin.
-1.0,Between 1977 and 1981, a total of five mills were closed and approximately 25,000 jobs were lost countywide.
0.0,Meetings of union officials and mill bosses were hurriedly set up in an attempt to persuade the powers that be to reconsider their statement.
0.0,However, it was clear that, in the words of USWA president Lloyd McBride, If you cant make a buck, you get out of the business.
-1.0,On that date Jennings Lambeth, president of Youngstown Sheet and Tube Company, announced that most of the steel companys Campbell Works would close.
0.0,If you cant make a buck, you get out of the business.
0.0,The closings meant the end of Youngstowns only real industry, the end of its population growth, and then end of economic progress.
0.0,Without the mills, people sought other places of employment in adjoining states or even other areas of the country.
0.0,Those that could afford to move did so; those that couldnt afford to move mostly ended up on the streets.
-1.0,Without an industrial or a residential base, commerce shrank considerably.
-1.0,It was becoming increasingly clear that without the industrial base provided by the mills, the city of Youngstown would soon become a ghost town, inhabited by those too poor or hopeful to escape.
0.0,The workers decided they needed to do something to save their city, and so they mobilized in a variety of ways.
0.0,Attempts to Save the Mills
0.0,The very first thing that the workers could do was to get up a petition to stop the shutdown, says Ed Mann, a local union leader and organizer.
0.0,to get up a petition to stop the shutdown,
0.0,The petition was circulated, eventually including thousands of signatures; it was then given to USWA representatives to present to President Carter in Washington.
0.0,However, the representatives were shunted to the side and ignored in Washington, since Youngstowns political influence had died with its industry.
0.0,The International chapter of the USWA had much more lobbying power, but they refused to support the local union members.
0.0,The petition was lost among paperwork and bureaucratic procedure.
0.0,Next, workers decided to form the Ecumenical Coalition, an organization of local religious groups which spearheaded the attempt to reopen the Youngstown works.
0.0,The Coalition drafter letters to the Lykes Company asking if a group of workers might purchase the mill and run it collectively.
-1.0,Although for other cities this would simply be a minor economic setback, for the people of Youngstown and the surrounding area, it meant disaster.
0.0,Lykes ignored the letters, so the Coalition turned once again to the federal government.
-1.0,Here, too, they were ignored.
0.0,The Coalition had no proper funds to buy the mills, so they could do nothing but sit back and watch as the mills closed.
0.0,Finally, following the shutdown of US Steels plant in 1980, local union leaders congregated outside the US Steel Headquarters in Youngstown.
0.0,They invited local people and politicians to witness the scene, then charged the Headquarters and took it over.
0.0,The workers stayed there until the next day, when US Steel declared that they were ready to talk about selling the mill.
0.0,Immediately after the workers left the building, US steel representatives told the local union leaders that they had changed their minds and were no longer interested in allowing the workers to purchase the mill.
-1.0,All these efforts eventually came to nothing, and Youngstowns steel mills remained closed.
0.0,These attempts to save the mills were hindered by several major factors, including the decline of the world steel market, which made American steel impossible to sell or export.
-1.0,The Decline of the World Market
0.0,The efforts to save the mills failed partly because the international market for steel had largely dried up.
0.0,In fact, American steel imports were beginning to outweigh exports.
0.0,Foreign steel was easier and more efficient to make, and was often of higher quality than domestic steel.
0.0,Mahoning County was a one-industry area, and the people of Youngstown, Struthers, Campbell, Boardman Township, and the numerous other small towns and villages in the area only had one main employer: the steel mills.
0.0,Foreign steel companies invested in their factories, updating their technology and replacing their equipment often.
0.0,This meant that foreign facilities were more modern and efficient than any plants in America, and therefore were able to export a more competitive product.
0.0,Foreign steel was also much cheaper.
0.0,Wage hikes, although they helped to improve living conditions of steel workers in the US, made American steel far more expensive.
0.0,You can mix them with a 30/30/40 mix of potting soil, worm casings and clay.
0.0,Or you could go out to the shed and grab a few handfuls of that sod mix you got at that estate sale last year and get to mixing.
0.0,NOTE: Cover your work area.
0.0,Dust can fly into your mouth and eyes very easily.
0.0,If the fertilizer in the mix is what I think it is, that wouldn't be pretty.
0.0,Use gloves to break up the soil with your fingers.
0.0,3. Make bombs.
0.0,Form the mix into balls of any size from sling-shot-pellet up to softball.
0.0,You're going to be throwing them.
0.0,Customize it yourself.
0.0,Mine were more or less matzoh-ball size and shape, out of habit.
0.0,This worked out pretty well.
0.0,Allow to dry overnight, or until they're solid enough for the next step.
0.0,4. Throw.
0.0,Today, I kept it simple.
0.0,I chose one abandoned property a few minutes from downtown, and two vacant lots.
0.0,The leftovers went onto the jungles alongside the freeway offramps.
0.0,First lesson learned -- you need at least two people to seedbomb from a vehicle .
0.0,The first responsibility should be driving safely.
-1.0,I found this hard to do while also avoiding cops, dealing with the camera and the car window, scoping out angles of approach for throwing, etc.
0.0,Seedbombing combines elements of childhood disgruntled mudbomb-hurling; the balance of meticulousness and zen that good gardeners possess; and my own forte, the invisibility and vigilance of a sniper.
-1.0,I ended up with a broken fingernail and dirt all over my lap.
0.0,Also, a perfect strike.
0.0,But you'll have to take my word because a camera at that moment would have been crazy.
0.0,Second Lesson -- keep the seedbombs in a shallow covered container .
0.0,You want both tidiness and easy access.
0.0,Plus, those things are crumbly.
0.0,I made eight; the last two were totally pulverized after being jostled in a paper bag for half an hour.
1.0,And the last lesson -- have fun .
0.0,It's play.
0.0,Seedbombing is a hit-or-miss way for change to take root, pun intended.
0.0,It's chlorophyll graffiti.
0.0,No one I know is getting digg'd or favrd yet for throwing color and scent around the ghetto.
0.0,Do it to see how it feels.
0.0,You may want to keep checking on your flowers (I promise I will) or you might get an idea to do something else completely unexpected (I did).
0.0,Enzo Angolini spike heels found by serendipity at St Paul's Thrift for $3.98.
0.0,Sexy, non?
0.0,For example, make smaller wildflower seedbombs and carefully 'plant' them in a meridian by making holes in the ground with your heel and then gently tamping the dirt over them with your sole.

0.0,Earth is my friend, like that old classmate who you keep forgetting to drop a note to on Facebook.
1.0,When I took a victory lap and hand-wash break in the mall, I was happy, not in a smug superior way, but in the knowledge that I had avenged myself against the whole Sunday-at-the-mall culture that I felt smothered by.
-1.0,There is one over-riding message to this -- Quit being such a goddamned perfectionist.
0.0,Yes, yes, I know, you know of much better places to never throw those seedbombs you haven't made.
0.0,You could get better soil if you put it on the shopping list.
-1.0,You undoubtedly write much better and could have a real serious article with awesome non-blurry pictures taken by a person who actually can get the timer to work for a goddamn change.

0.0,Cycling is a thing of the past: a sport, a hobby, but rarely a mode of transportation.
0.0,Want to get involved?

0.0,Can't find a bike community?
0.0,Start your own!

0.0,But farming on the Outer Cape is the sort of Sisyphian challenge that can wear anybody out.
0.0,The hard truth: The soil of North Truro is not strong enough to support agriculture.
0.0,Without fertilization, it deteriorates shockingly fast.
0.0,David points out a patch of sand with a thin strip of fertile loam along the edge.
0.0,Last season it was a fertile veggie bed -- but it was left un-fertilized as an experiment.

-1.0,Last year's rich loam is now useless sand.
0.0,It's always been this way in North Truro.
0.0,The Outer Cape is really just a spit of sand -- but still, farmers lived here for generations.
0.0,How?
0.0,Salt marsh hay.
0.0,There used to be a local tradition in this area: at each spring tide , the local community would head out to the bogs and marshes to harvest the grasses.
0.0,This was called "salt marsh haying".
0.0,"salt marsh haying"
0.0,Salt marsh hay has no weed seeds, and it doesn't compact as heavily as other types of hay.
0.0,This makes it an excellent and bountiful source of compost, and it was used for generations as a soil enricher.
0.0,But haying had to happen regularly, says David: "There's so much oxygen in this soil, any added compost gets burned up in six weeks.
0.0,"There's so much oxygen in this soil, any added compost gets burned up in six weeks. All the nutrients get depleted."
-1.0,All the nutrients get depleted."
0.0,The only way to keep things going here is to keep a steady flow of compost coming in.
0.0,That means truckloads of hay, and that means a lot of work.
0.0,Last year, David and Arthur brought in a semi truck loaded with leaf mulch.
0.0,It worked -- but it cost money, and it disappeared fast into the hungry ground.
0.0,Not a long-term plan.
0.0,Without that community support, it's nearly impossible for him to harvest hay often enough to keep the farm green.

0.0,Kitchen Equipment.
0.0,Woks and any other gadgets essential for Chinese cookery make good purchases.
0.0,Department stores sell all sorts of intriguing kitchen equipment.
0.0,Leather Goods.
0.0,Large shops on the fashionable thoroughfares tend to be more expensive than smaller family shops tucked away in the side streets.
0.0,Locally made items do not live up to their European models.
0.0,However, the leather garment industry is growing, and there is a wide range of locally produced leather accessories, all at extremely attractive prices.
0.0,For European imports, you will pay top dollar.
0.0,Musical, Audio, and Video Equipment.
0.0,Hong Kong has a vast range of the most high-tech audio-visual, sound, and screen equipment.
0.0,While its no longer the bargain shopping destination it once was, there are still some good buys to be had.
0.0,Before purchasing, visitors should make sure of compatibility with systems in their own countries.
0.0,Be sure to look around and compare before buying.
0.0,Whatever you buy, you may be able to work out a discount.
0.0,Ready-to-wear Clothes.
0.0,Hong Kongs shops carry almost every recognizable European and many American labels, from top-end designers to the moderately priced or trendy.
0.0,Nathan Road, Central, and the hotel malls are places to look.
0.0,There are still a great many factory outlet stores with reasonable prices.
0.0,Youll also find bargain clothes for sale at the markets and on push-carts.
0.0,Tailoring.
0.0,Tailor-made clothes are not as popular in Hong Kong as they were in the past, but hundreds of shops still remain.
0.0,Local tailors are experts when it comes to producing custom-tailored garments for both men and women, and are also adept at copying patterns.
0.0,In choosing a tailor, look for HKTA membership.
0.0,Stores do not open until 10am or later, but shopping goes on into the evening, up to 9:30pm.
0.0,Many tailors have Web sites or are listed on Web sites.
0.0,Tea.
0.0,Shops all over town will sell you gift tins of exotic blends.
0.0,If you want to learn something about tea, go to the Tea Shop at 149 Hollywood Road, or the Moon Garden Tea House at 5 Hoi Ping Road, Causeway Bay.
0.0,The owners will brew up a pot so you can taste before making a choice.
0.0,Watches.
0.0,The saying Time is money is quite literally true in Hong Kong: more is spent on watches and clocks here than on cameras and optical goods.
0.0,An enormous variety of makes and models are on sale.
0.0,Be sure to get the manufacturers guarantee stamped or signed if you buy a watch.
0.0,Entertainment
0.0,Day and night, the action goes on in this vibrant city.
0.0,Most shops are open seven days a week.
0.0,Hong Kong Diary published weekly by HKTA tells whats happening in the arts.
0.0,Hong Kong Life is published by the Hong Kong Standard on Sunday, and the South China Morning Post has an entertainment section on Friday.
0.0,Culture buffs are well catered to, and there is always a varied program of events, ranging from world-class concerts to local amateur dramatic productions.
0.0,A highlight of the arts calendar is the annual Hong Kong Arts Festival, a three-week dose of international culture in February, with concerts, recitals, plays, jazz, Chinese opera, and innovative productions put on by leading talent from both East and West.
0.0,Shops in Central are an exception; they generally close at 6pm and are not open on Sunday.
0.0,Tickets for the shows must be reserved well in advance.
0.0,The Festival of Asian Arts takes place every other October, bringing to Hong Kong for two weeks orchestras, dance groups, opera, and drama companies from all over Asia.
0.0,There are more than 30 cinemas in Hong Kong, and the latest Western releases are shown in some of the larger ones.
0.0,English-language films have Chinese subtitles.
0.0,The Hong Kong International Film Festival takes place in April.
0.0,More than 200 films from all over the world are shown at this two-week event.
0.0,The only holiday on which all commerce comes to a halt is the Chinese New Year in January or February.
0.0,Ask at City Hall center about advance reservations.
0.0,The Performing Arts
0.0,Performance Venues.
0.0,The theaters in the Hong Kong Cultural Center in Tsim Sha Tsui are the main venues for concerts and opera.
0.0,Other performance centers are the City Hall cultural complex, with exhibition halls and theaters that present concerts, plays, and films; the Hong Kong Academy for the Performing Arts with two major theaters for dance, drama, and concert performances; and the Hong Kong Arts Centre in Wan Chai, where both local and visiting groups perform.
0.0,Other centers for concerts, plays, and entertainment are Sha Tin Town Hall and Tsuen Wan Town Hall in the New Territories.
0.0,Larger arenas, including the Queen Elizabeth Stadium, the Hong Kong Coliseum, and the Ko Shan Theater in Kowloon play host to various concerts, pop concerts, sporting events, and variety shows.
0.0,Classical Music.
0.0,The Hong Kong Chinese Orchestra performs new and traditional works; a wide assortment of traditional and Chinese instruments are featured.
0.0,The Hong Kong Philharmonic Orchestra was founded in 1975.
0.0,Buyer Beware.
0.0,Under its conductor, David Atherton, it offers Western classical works and new works by Chinese composers in a September-to-June season.
-1.0,Be aware that name brands, including electronics, are sometimes fakes, glass may be sold as jade, and that antique you bought may have been made last night.
0.0,Chinese Opera.
0.0,Cantonese opera is alive and well in Hong Kong, and the two other forms, Beijing and Kun, are sometimes presented.
0.0,To most foreigners, this unique art form is likely to be inscrutable at first exposure, but everyone can appreciate the spectacle and the elaborate, glittering costumes.
0.0,Although the music may seem strange to the unaccustomed ear, it certainly wont put you to sleep; cymbals and drums guarantee your alertness.
0.0,Dance.
0.0,Hong Kongs three professional dance companiesthe Hong Kong Ballet Company, the Hong Kong Dance Company, and the newer City Contemporary Dance Companyperform regularly, often at the Hong Kong Academy for the Performing Arts.
0.0,Theater.
0.0,The two leading local troupes, the Chung Ying Theatre Company and the Hong Kong Repertory Theatre, perform in Cantonese; there are English-language performances at the Fringe Club theaters, 2 Lower Albert Road, in Central.
0.0,Puppet Shows.
0.0,The classic Chinese puppet is the shadow puppet, manipulated behind a screen by three rods, but hand puppet and marionette shows are also on offer, often for free at public parks and playgrounds.
0.0,Nightlife
0.0,Hong Kong by night can suit any tasteriotous, sedate, raw, or cultured.
0.0,Note that sometimes there is a cover charge of HK$50 to HK$200 at clubs, which may or may not include a couple of drinks.
0.0,There are nightclubs in the principal hotels, with bands, dancing, and floor shows.
0.0,Always ask for a receipt that records information about the item, and if you buy an antique, be sure to get a certificate of authentication.
0.0,Jazz fans will find live jazz presented by international artists at the Jazz Club and Bar, 2/F, 34-36 DAgular, Central; and at the Blue Note in the Kowloon Shangri-La Hotel in Tsim Sha Tsui.
0.0,The Frin ge Club, 21 Lower Albert Road, Central, is Hong Kongs best-known alternate entertainment venue, with jazz, rock, and other live music, in addition to a gallery for visual arts.
0.0,Bars with views and live music include Sky Lounge in the Sheraton Hotel and Towers, Tsim Sha Tsui; and Cyrano in the Island Shangri-La in Pacific Place.
0.0,Pubs are numerous.
0.0,In Tsim Sha Tsui, Ned Kellys Last Stand on Ashley Road is an Aussie institution; Delaneys, 71-77 Peking Road, is one of Hong Kongs enduring Irish pubs.
0.0,The clubs and bars of Wan Chai, long the center of seedy nightlife, have become almost respectable.
0.0,Joe Bananas, 23 Luard Road, is a Wan Chai mainstay for all-night partying.
0.0,Ricks Cafe, 78-82 Jaffe Road, is a long-time disco thats still popular.
0.0,A lot of the raunchy action has moved across the harbor to Tsim Sha Tsui East; this is also where youll find pricey hostess clubs, popular with Japanese tourists, but definitely not for those on a budget.
0.0,Todays trendy spot is Soho (SOuth of HOllywood) around Hollywood Road, Elgin, and Stauton streets.
0.0,Soho, along with the Lan Kwai Fong area, is popular with chuppies (Hong Kong yuppies) and has a lively bar scene.
0.0,Causeway Bay also has a variety of bars and clubs.
0.0,Needless to say, avoid peddlers who approach you on the street and offer to take you to wondrous bargains.
0.0,TOTTs, in the Excelsior Hotel, is a restaurant with live music and dancing and a harbor view.
0.0,Japanese karaoke bars have now become extremely popular with the locals.
0.0,There are a number of these on Chatham Road South and around Cameron Street in Tsim Sha Tsui.
0.0,The most typical of these are harbor cruises, usually including dinner and dancing on board an air-conditioned floating nightclub.
0.0,There are evening bus tours that include visits to a restaurant and night spots; some tours combine a Chinese banquet with a visit to an open-air market and the panorama from Victoria Peak.
0.0,Beaches.
0.0,In subtropical Hong Kong you can swim from April to early November.
0.0,There are more than 40 beaches in Hong Kong that are free to the public.
0.0,Most have lifeguards on duty from April to October, changing rooms, toilets, and snack stands.
0.0,On Hong Kong Island, Repulse Bay is the most popular; others are Shek O on the east coast and Stanley and Deep Water Bay on the south coast.
0.0,They are very crowded, especially on summer weekends.
0.0,On the outlying islands, Cheung Chau and Cheung Sha are on Lantau, and Hung Shing Ye and Lo So Shing on Lamma; inquire about water pollution levels.
0.0,The large department stores have fixed prices, but elsewhere you should ask whether there is a discount, especially if you buy several items in one shop.
0.0,The Hong Kong Golf Club (Tel. 2812 7070) welcomes visitors to its three 18-hole courses at Fanling in the New Territories, or the 9-hole course at Deep Water Bay.
0.0,The Discovery Bay Golf Club on Lantau island (Tel. 2987 7273) has an 18-hole Robert Trent Jones Jr. course, open to visitors Monday, Tuesday, and Friday.
0.0,Many Hong Kong residents and visitors take the express train to Guangzhou to play at the Guangzhou Luhu Golf and Country Club (Tel. 2317 1933 in Hong Kong or 020-8350 7777).

0.0,Hiking.
0.0,In the New Territories the famous MacLehose Trail stretches 97 km (60 miles) from Sai Kung Peninsula to Tuen Mun.
0.0,The Lantau Trail is a 69-km (43-mile) circular trail on Lantau Island that begins and ends at Silvermine Bay.
0.0,Both trails are divided into smaller segments of varying difficulty.
0.0,Maps of hiking trails are available at the Government Publications Center, Low Block, Government Offices, 66 Queensway in Central.

0.0,Jogging.

0.0,Membership imposes an obligation to maintain standards of both quality and service, and provides dissatisfied customers with an officially recognized channel for redressing complaints; the number to call is Tel. 2508 1234.
0.0,Pick up a copy of HKTAs The Official Dining, Entertainment & Shopping Directory in which all member stores are listed.

0.0,Many stores will pack and ship purchases.

0.0,Packages sent to the US or to Europe generally take six to eight weeks by surface mail, and one week by airmail.
0.0,Shopping Areas.
0.0,Major shopping areas are Tsim Sha Tsui in Kowloon, especially along Nathan Road; Central on Hong Kong Island, particularly for upscale designer goods; Causeway Bay for slightly better prices; and the Hollywood Road area.
0.0,On photographic equipment, electronic goods, and watches, you avoid the luxury tax payable in your home country.
0.0,Department Stores.
0.0,Look for Lane Crawford Ltd., an upscale store with branches at Pacific Place, 70 Queens Road, and Harbour City; Wing On, one of the oldest in Hong Kong; Marks and Spencer; and the Japanese department stores, Mitsukoshi, Sobo, and Seibu.
0.0,Malls.
0.0,Hong Kong is full of giant malls.
0.0,Harbour City, just west of the Star Ferry Terminal in Tsim Sha Tsui is one of the largest; Pacific Place, 88 Queensway, is Centrals biggest mall, with retail outlets and department stores; Times Square is a collection of retail outlets in Causeway Bay.
0.0,In addition, most top-line hotels have upscale malls full of designer boutiques.
0.0,Factory Outlets.
0.0,These stores sell excess stock or factory overruns.
0.0,Hong Kong is no longer a factory outlet center since much of its clothing manufacturing has moved elsewhere.
0.0,There are factory showrooms in the Pedder Building, 12 Pedder Street, in Central.
0.0,Markets.
0.0,Markets are the places to use your bargaining skills.
0.0,Hong Kongs most famous and colorful market is the Temple Street Night Market near the Jordan MTR stop.
0.0,Every conceivable kind of goods is sold here: clothing, all kinds of electronics, CDs, souvenirs, crafts, and jewelry.
0.0,Specialty goods and souvenirs, often handmade, come from Hong Kong and elsewhere in China.
0.0,Stanley Market is located on Hong Kongs southern coast, and is well-known for all kinds of clothing, including silk and cashmere.
0.0,Bargain, and carefully examine any merchandise you buy here.
0.0,The Jade Market, on Kansu Street in Yau Ma Tei, is known for both jade and freshwater pearls.
0.0,This is not the place to make expensive purchases, but its great for inexpensive pendants, earrings, and gifts.
0.0,What to Buy
0.0,Antiques.
0.0,Hollywood Road in the Mid-Levels above Central is the most famous antiques street in Hong Kong.
0.0,Look for fine Chinese bronzes, embroidery, lacquerware and porcelain, tomb figures, and wood carvings, among other possibilities.
0.0,The experts point out that it is not age alone that determines a Chinese antiques valuethe dynasties of the past had their creative ups and downs.
0.0,Custom-made garments by skillful Hong Kong tailors are still much in demand and cost less than elsewhere for comparable garments.
0.0,For serious antiques, try Honeychurch Antiques at no. 29 for furniture and silver, Tai Sing Company at 122 for porcelain.
0.0,For fun you can visit the Low Price Shop at no. 47 or the Cat Street crafts stores and flea market.
0.0,Brocades and Silks.
0.0,Fabrics from China are a bargain and well worth taking home.
-1.0,Inflation has taken its toll in Hong Kong.
0.0,For fabrics, also try Western Market, Morrison Street, in Central.
0.0,Photo buffs know that Hong Kong is the place to buy some of the worlds most advanced photographic equipment, and there are some real bargains around.
0.0,However, be sure you compare prices and models before buying.
0.0,Two reliable places to start looking in Lan Kwai Fong are Photo Scientific in the Eurasia Building and Hing Lee Camera Company, 25 Lyndhurst Terrace.
0.0,Carpets and Rugs.
0.0,Hong Kong is a mecca for Chinese hand-knotted wool carpets and silk rugs.
0.0,Hong Kongs stores are usually able to arrange shipment.
0.0,Caravan at 65 Hollywood Road and the shops in The Silk Road at Ocean Center in Tsim Sha Tsui are good places to start looking.
0.0,Note that alcohol and tobacco are both exceptions to Hong Kongs duty-free regime and are subject to tax.
0.0,China (Porcelain).
0.0,In Hong Kong you can have a plate, or even a whole dinner service, hand-painted to your own design.
0.0,Factories in Kowloon and the New Territories, producing traditional and modern china, are geared to entertain and instruct visiting tourists; prices are appealing.
0.0,Two of the largest places to go are the Wah Tung China Company in the Grand Marine Industrial Building in Aberdeen; and the Overjoy Porcelain Factory in Block B of the Kwai Hing Industrial Building, Kwai Chung, in the New Territories.
0.0,In antiques shops, look for highly valued porcelains from China.
0.0,Note that because of the duty-free situation, good bargains may be found in European china, including Spode and Wedgwood.
0.0,Electronics.
0.0,The latest gadgets are sometimes available in Hong Kong before anywhere else.
0.0,Before you begin shopping, pick up HKTAs Shopping Guide to Consumer Electronics. 
0.0,Prices on electronics have risen in the past two years; check prices at home before you buy here.
0.0,Nathan Road has many electronics shops.
0.0,Also check out Star Computer City in the Star House near the Star Ferry terminal.
0.0,Youll find that prices are about the same in Hong Kong Central and Kowloon, and somewhat cheaper in Causeway Bay, which caters to local shopping.
0.0,Furniture.
0.0,The choice ranges from traditional hand-carved Chinese rosewood furniture to well-made reproductions of modern Western styles.
0.0,Rattan furniture is highly popular.
0.0,Hollywood Road has several furniture shops.
0.0,Queens Road East in Wan Chai is a furniture manufacturing and retail area.
0.0,Jade.
0.0, Good for the health is just one of the many magical qualities that are attributed to these beautiful emerald-green or turquoise stones.
0.0,Real jade is extremely expensive, and you may be offered counterfeit jade, which looks exactly like the genuine article.
0.0,Some people say you can test the authenticity by touchreal jade feels smooth and cool.
0.0,Alternatively, you can shine a lamp on the stonereal jade shows no reflected light.
0.0,Better still, go shopping with an expert.
0.0,Jewelry.
0.0,Thanks to the duty-free situation, prices in Hong Kong are lower than they are in some other places.
0.0,You can buy gemstones loose or set, or have them made up to your own design.
0.0,Popular purchases include diamonds and freshwater pearls.
0.0,If you do plan to buy jewelry, be sure to consult the Shopping Guide to Jewellery published by the Hong Kong Tourist Authority to find a reputable dealer.
